<span id="freeTextContainer12107519670160430958">The first book in The Shades of London series, The Name of the Star sucked me right in and held tightly. I have never been so thrilled to have the next book-in-the-series- already on hand. One book with these dynamic, compelling and wickedly funny characters was simply not enough.<br/><br/>Because Ms. Johnson could write an entertaining cereal box, I'll share a few of my favorite quotes from this book rather than give a detailed review in an effort to lure you in.<br/><br/> <br/> “Something about her suggested that her </span>
  <span id="freeText12107519670160430958" style="display:none">The first book in The Shades of London series, The Name of the Star sucked me right in and held tightly. I have never been so thrilled to have the next book-in-the-series- already on hand. One book with these dynamic, compelling and wickedly funny characters was simply not enough.<br /><br />Because Ms. Johnson could write an entertaining cereal box, I'll share a few of my favorite quotes from this book rather than give a detailed review in an effort to lure you in.<br /><br /> <br /> “Something about her suggested that her leisure activities included wrestling large woodland animals and banging bricks together.” <br /><br /> “He told me scary Jack the Ripper facts, and I had the sudden need to make out with him until I ran out of breath.”<br /><br /> “You assume everyone you see is alive.”<br /><br /> “Some things are so bad that once you’ve been through them, you don’t have to explain your reasons to anyone.”<br /><br /> “I’d been ripped by the Ripper. I was a walking T-shirt slogan.”<br /></span>

<div id="review_1389531118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389531118" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389531118?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it

The story moved along nicely and built up a good deal of suspense along the way, and the cast of supporting characters were nicely developed and had legitimate voices of their own.           <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399256608" href="/book/show/9802372-the-name-of-the-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=library">library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040722327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6929716348953273673"><b>You can also find my review on my blog <a href='http://thatgirlbookworm.blogspot.ca/2015/08/book-review-29-name-of-star-by-maureen.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>thatgirlbookworm</a></b><br/><br/>Just a fun fact about me: I don't read book blurbs. Whether I've been anticipating the book for a long time, or it's a book I've never heard of, I don't read blurbs. I find they give away too many little spoilers that I would much rather find out. Therefore I am a judge a book by it's cover type of person.<br/>That being said, I chose to read this entirely because I loved Maureen Johnson's story in Let It Snow. That was my entire reason and there</span>
  <span id="freeText6929716348953273673" style="display:none"><b>You can also find my review on my blog <a href="http://thatgirlbookworm.blogspot.ca/2015/08/book-review-29-name-of-star-by-maureen.html" rel="nofollow noopener">thatgirlbookworm</a></b><br /><br />Just a fun fact about me: I don't read book blurbs. Whether I've been anticipating the book for a long time, or it's a book I've never heard of, I don't read blurbs. I find they give away too many little spoilers that I would much rather find out. Therefore I am a judge a book by it's cover type of person.<br />That being said, I chose to read this entirely because I loved Maureen Johnson's story in Let It Snow. That was my entire reason and therefore I had no idea what this book was about.<br />To put it mildly, I was extremely ecstatic when I realized that this was a Jack the Ripper story. I love to study Serial Killers, I read biographies and true crime books constantly and I study them in school so when I started this I was extremely excited. It did not disappoint.<br />Johnson managed to include this really unique idea and plot point into a story that I already liked. I would have loved to just read about a Jack the Ripper copycat, but the extra plots and storylines she included were amazing.<br />Her character building is so well done, I can see how talented Maureen Johnson is just from this one book. Rory is a strong character, and on top of that, she had about 10 minor characters who all managed to have their own personality, which is often times rare to see. <br />I will say, one thing that I found refreshing was the lack of love story. Yes there's a minor love interest, nothing major, but it doesn't dominate the storyline. Not even close, and I like that. Not that I don't love some good fluff once in a while, but I really wanted to read a book about something else with no romance and this definitely delivered.<br />Overall, a really really unique book that was well done. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6929716348953273673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399256608" href="/book/show/9802372-the-name-of-the-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591131842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3799964232502981376"><b>
  <i>"Fear can't hurt you. When it washes over you, give it no power. It's a snake with no venom."</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/jack%20the%20ripper' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417743i/826557._SX540_.jpg' alt='jack the ripper photo: Jack the Ripper ripper.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Setting:</b>Whitechapel, London, England; 2011<br/><br/><b>Coverly Love?:</b>Yes! It has a certain mysterious quality to it that made me want to read it. The fog and the faint outline of a London street is a nice touch to the ghostly feel of the novel. However, I'm still trying to figure out who the two people on the cover are supposed to be. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I think the girl lying down might be one of the Ripper's vic</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3799964232502981376" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Fear can't hurt you. When it washes over you, give it no power. It's a snake with no venom."</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/jack%20the%20ripper" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417743i/826557._SX540_.jpg" alt="jack the ripper photo: Jack the Ripper ripper.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Setting:</b>Whitechapel, London, England; 2011<br><br><b>Coverly Love?:</b>Yes! It has a certain mysterious quality to it that made me want to read it. The fog and the faint outline of a London street is a nice touch to the ghostly feel of the novel. However, I'm still trying to figure out who the two people on the cover are supposed to be. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think the girl lying down might be one of the Ripper's victims, but I don't think the man pictured is the Ripper. Or if he is, it's a very poor character impersonator. He's supposed to be bald!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Plot:</b>Aurora"Rory"Deveaux is an American exchange student at Wexford, a prestigious London boarding school. It also happens to be right smack dab in the middle of Whitechapel, where the world's most infamous serial killer committed his murders back in the late 1800s. Amd it seems that there is a copycat roaming loose in modern day London, killing victims exactly as the Ripper did. Who is this Ripper? Can he be stopped?<br><br>I think the author did an amazing job with the plotline. It was a very original, fresh take on Ripper mythology, and I quite like reading about Jack the Ripper theories, considering there has been no hard proof as to who he really is, and I don't think there ever will be. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But when we do find out who the murderer really is, it was a bit confusing as to why he did what he did, since he never really gave a clear reason <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The ending defenitely was dramatic and ended with a bang. And no unecessary cliffhangers!<br><br><b>Characters:</b>Rory is a very likable protagonist, someone who you could instantly see as beng the fun, goofy BFF you can gossip and confide in. She didn't have the "Atittude" at all, and always had something quick and witty to say.<br><br>Jazza is Rory's roomate and was also very likable. She was a bit quirky, but reminded me very much of me and my own best friend, and our dynamic together. I'm more of the shy friend, and she's more outgoing like Rory.<br><br>Boo, Callum, and Steven are also major players in this novel, helping Rory discover and come to terms with her newfound power. They are very loyal and caring, if a bit rough around the edges.<br><br>Other colorful characters include "Call Me Claudia", the headmistress, Charlotte and Jerome, the head girl and boy, and Alistair, the Smiths loving, punk hairdoed kid who always chills on the library. <br><br><b>Pros:</b>I loved Rory!! She was the one of the most likable protagonists I've read about, and she was a geniunly funny person to read about. Alistair cracked me up, and the mythology of the book was very clever. I also appreciated how human she made the characters. She didn't try to make them perfect, but at the same time didn't give them any major, unrealistic flaws. And the setting of London and how she described it made me feel like I was actually there.<br><br><b>Cons:</b>I feel that the character of Charlotte was specifically created for the sole reason of Rory to have a nemesis (other then the murderer, of course). But really, she didn't do anything quote "bad", and I honestly couldn't understand where all the animosity came from (unless I'm missing something important here). And I was a bit confused as to <i>why</i> the copycat killer did the gruesome murders. There was no specific reason, perse, and it was a bit confusing to me.<br><br><b>Love Triangle?:</b>Nope!<br><br><b>Insta-Love?:</b>Nope!<br><br><b>Romance?:</b>Yes! Rory and Jerome. Their romance was very sweet and didn't annoy me at all. Jerome was surprisingly normal for a YA male love interest. Too many of them are described as "brooding, tortured soul", or "devestatingly handsome". He was cute and a little dorky (with his Ripper obsession). And I loved how the romance didn't overpower the story. Rory was perfectly fine without him, and didn't feel the need to be around him all the time. <br><br><b>Conclusion:</b>An enjoyable, mysterious take on the Ripper mystery. If you love ghost stories, mysteries, or anything having to do with London, pick this up. Also recommended for those who like funny female protagonists who are not shrinking violets. I will definitely be continuing with this series to see where Rory is headed next.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_249817011" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249817011" />
    <a title="rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2499261-rachel"><img alt="rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572660600p2/2499261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249817011?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel" href="/user/show/2499261-rachel">rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399256608" href="/book/show/9802372-the-name-of-the-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2499261-rachel?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2499261-rachel?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2499261-rachel?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249817011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8039773325159589139">Oh dear. Disappointment! One of my least favorite feelings. When Hannah first told me about this book, I had stars in my eyes: Maureen Johnson, who charmed me with <i>The Bermudez Triangle</i> and makes me giggle on Twitter sometimes, writing a teen book about Jack the Ripper? It seemed sort of like the pairing of brownies and soda -- gee, I don't know how this will work! But each of those things on their own? Yummy decay.<br/><br/>The cover of this book, though -- I felt such apprehension. Why is it glittery? W</span>
  <span id="freeText8039773325159589139" style="display:none">Oh dear. Disappointment! One of my least favorite feelings. When Hannah first told me about this book, I had stars in my eyes: Maureen Johnson, who charmed me with <i>The Bermudez Triangle</i> and makes me giggle on Twitter sometimes, writing a teen book about Jack the Ripper? It seemed sort of like the pairing of brownies and soda -- gee, I don't know how this will work! But each of those things on their own? Yummy decay.<br /><br />The cover of this book, though -- I felt such apprehension. Why is it glittery? Why is Jack the Ripper such a stud? I know teens are swooning over wacky things like werewolves these days, but do publishers think teens would really swoon if wacky Jacky charmed ladies before disembowling them? But I went for it anyway and there is, thankfully, no surprise romance in this book. (There is a very, very incidental romance between main character Rory and this boy at her boarding school, which has nothing to do with anything except the sake of giving us some kissin' scenes.) <br /><br />The first half of the book is mostly very detailed scenes of a transplanted American girl from the deep South acclimating to her new, posh English boarding school &amp; schoolmates, with a grisly Ripper knockoff murder here and there. I really loved this part of the book. Place and character being established, Ripper tidbits for those who didn't spend their ten year old years gawking at their dad's true crime collection and couldn't name or picture the big five victims and their crime scenes offhand (you're welcome for that bit of skeeve).<br /><br />But then...ghosts. Yeah, I don't know. Ghosts and ghost hunting police and killing ghosts with cell phones and villains revealing dastardly plans that actually have very little to do with Jack the Ripper at all, and it's like wait, what was the purpose of spending 10 pages on field hockey and other Britishisms back there if this is what it's going to eventually come to? The paranormal plot-heaviness makes even the Jack the Ripper element of the story seem unnecessary, tacked on to scandalize and to reel in creepos like me. <br /><br />It all felt like Johnson really wanted to write a book about <i>London</i> and really wanted to write a book about <i>boarding school</i> and really wanted to write a book about <i>Jack</i> and really wanted to write about <i>ghost police</i> and it all got mashed into this thing that is like the oddly paced result of a writer's group prompt. Libba Bray's <i>Beauty Queens</i> felt that way too, but at least that book was cohesive. I mean, it even seemed like Rory only had a personality for the first part of this book and totally lost it once the ghosty action started happening. How?! Why?! :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="8039773325159589139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_948101268" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/948101268" />
    <a title="Xueting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4691420-xueting"><img alt="Xueting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584371487p2/4691420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/948101268?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xueting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xueting" href="/user/show/4691420-xueting">Xueting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399256608" href="/book/show/9802372-the-name-of-the-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4691420-xueting?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4691420-xueting?shelf=unputdownable">unputdownable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948101268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12685484247306368404">This book is so much fun and incredibly thrilling! I'm glad Maureen Johnson mixed in lots of wry humour, it's true to her own personality and makes her protagonist Rory more unique. For someone from neither England nor the United States, I was intrigued by the depth of historical research Johnson did and I never seriously fell out of the loop with the references because she explains them well without overdoing it patronisingly, yay! There were quite a few big twists too, more than I expected fro</span>
  <span id="freeText12685484247306368404" style="display:none">This book is so much fun and incredibly thrilling! I'm glad Maureen Johnson mixed in lots of wry humour, it's true to her own personality and makes her protagonist Rory more unique. For someone from neither England nor the United States, I was intrigued by the depth of historical research Johnson did and I never seriously fell out of the loop with the references because she explains them well without overdoing it patronisingly, yay! There were quite a few big twists too, more than I expected from a common paranormal-themed story, also yay. That slight cliffhanger was also brilliant! It gave me a warm fuzzy sense of closure to the whole exciting story and really makes me already start guessing what the next stories would be about. On that note, I have to also praise the pacing of the story - it started out a little slow but it was a relaxing read that set up a bunch of extremely significant plot points for later, which totally came whooshing like a rollercoaster!! <br /><br />I read some other reviews, and I agree with them about some pretty big logical gaps in the story, but they didn't scream out at me so much that I got distracted by the actual storyline nor did they turn me off the whole book. Cut Maureen some slack! Especially for the fantastic job she did with the more important parts of the book, like her depth of planning and her writing.<br /><br />Anyway, I really recommend this one! Can't wait to read the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12685484247306368404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gDnlwZFlxLdCeBql9BXNGtsgETJFd5NmBr1rFrX+QzBemDnj1QJiysFU6WAkliAHtmeREBsRHas7pLN7ZuEm9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gZjmWgcqhHIi+vck0Izv9FR/if3CBuElpBJ1GyF+UX9fOTp4Q00iD6HWBOEADwLpOTgJ35xgb+iZC6128mE0uA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_31750999'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31750999-the-go-between?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Go-Between<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/39430.Veronica_Chambers?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Veronica Chambers<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.21 avg rating &mdash; 740 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2017\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer17904715583314721122\">5 hours and 30 minutes\n\nFans of Jane the Virgin will find much to love about this coming-of-age novel from bestselling author Veronica Chambers, who with humor and humanity explores issues of identity and belonging in a world that is ever-changing. \n<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17904715583314721122\" style=\"display:none\">5 hours and 30 minutes\n\nFans of Jane the Virgin will find much to love about this coming-of-age novel from bestselling author Veronica Chambers, who with humor and humanity explores issues of identity and belonging in a world that is ever-changing. \n\nShe is the envy of every teenage girl in Mexico City. Her mother is a glamorous telenovela actress. Her father is the go-to voice-over talent for blockbuster films. Hers is a world of private planes, chauffeurs, paparazzi and gossip columnists. Meet Camilla del Valle Cammi to those who know her best. \n\nWhen Cammi s mom gets cast in an American television show and the family moves to LA, things change, and quickly.
